First tribe to release their tribe's banner wins fishing gear, and the last tribe to do so will vote someone out. He describes the next challenge as dealing with the devices, but instead of using the quipu as a counting device, one person on each tribe will be using them as a key to a block puzzle. Each tribe has a wall consisting of twenty blocks sticking out of it that can be pushed and pulled into it. Each block needs to be pushed or pulled a certain amount to open up a space inside the wall that a ball can roll through. The first tribe to roll a ball behind every block in a single run wins immunity and comfort in the form of blankets. The second tribe to do so only wins immunity, and the third tribe goes to tribal council. Quipu Readers: $c[Rhett], $o[Ashleia], $q[Paula] Puzzle Solvers: $c[Buddy, Jennifer, Lisa, Louie] $o[Candace, Jarrett, Min-Ji, Rocky] $q[Jackie, Khall, Monty, Vaclav] Sit-outs: $c[Denine], $o[Saul] At the last second, the quipu readers are given a cruel twist - their quipu each have 24 strings, each of the puzzle solvers is given a number that matches the number of a string that should be ignored, and they cannot use words to tell the reader which strings are to be ignored. Two members from each tribe will need to collect bags of rocks and run them to a conveyer belt, where two more members will manually crank a conveyor belt to move the rocks to the thrower. The thrower will open the bags and attempt to break all nine tiles with the rocks inside. First tribe to do so wins immunity and will have a latrine installed at their camp, the second tribe will only win immunity, and the third-place tribe will go to tribal council. Bag Collectors: $c[Denine and Louie], $o[Ashleia and Saul], $q[Khall and Paula] Conveyor Belt Crankers: $c[Buddy and Jennifer], $o[Jarrett and Rocky], $q[Monty and Vaclav] Throwers: $c[Rhett], $o[Candace], $q[Jackie] Chalpe is quickly weighed down by Louie tripping immediately upon the challenge starting, leaving Denine to pick up the slack. On the far end of a pool of water about 20 meters long is a pair of two platforms. Contestants must climb a ladder, and smash a tile hanging in front of them with a wooden baton to release a key. They must then swim back with the key and tag in the next person. There are five keys per tribe. Once all keys are returned, the final player must use all five keys to open a locked chest and use the letter tiles inside to spell out a phrase. First tribe to spell out the phrase wins two egg-laying chickens and a rooster. The sixth player has to direct the rest of their tribe to finish the puzzle. First tribe to complete the puzzle wins immunity. Both tribes quickly agree on an order. They have to balance on their toes in order to hold a wooden block upright between the top of the frame and their head. If a contestant lets their block drop, or touches either side of their frame, they are out of the challenge. Last one standing wins immunity. Everyone takes to balancing fairly easily, at first. Candace clasps her hands together and begins to hum, and Rocky grumbles. Paula falls after only a couple minutes. Not long after, Louie's heels sink, and his block falls.
